2024, CIVIL APPEAL NOS. 11568-11569 OF 2024, CIVIL
APPEAL NO. 11571 OF 2024, CIVIL APPEAL NO. 11570 OF
2024 AND CIVIL APPEAL NO. 11572 OF 2024
1) The issue that falls for consideration in this batch
of cases is whether the termination of teachers appointed
by the Office of the District Basic Education Officer,
Shahjahanpur  (hereinafter,  “the  Basic  Education
Officer”), pursuant to the interim directions issued by
the High Court of Judicature at Allahabad (hereinafter,
“the High Court”) in Writ Petition (C) No. 2906 of 2013,
later converted into a Public Interest Litigation, can be
sustained. Though, the Public Interest Litigation has
since  been  dismissed  in  default  by  order  dated
24.03.2026.  The  further  question  is  whether  such
19

--- Page 24 ---
termination, effected without affording the opportunity
to the affected teachers in respect of the allegations
levelled against them, can nonetheless be maintained by
upholding the impugned order of the High Court.
2) The litigation before us has had a long and somewhat
chequered history. A brief reference to the relevant
facts is necessary to appreciate the controversy at hand.
The services of the appellants came to be terminated
after show cause notices were issued on different dates;
alleging inter alia, that their B.Ed. degrees and mark-
sheets were forged or tampered. In some cases, it was
alleged that the enrolment numbers were not reflected in
the mark-sheets. The show cause notices were based on the
interim progress report dated 14.08.2017 of the Special
Investigation Team (hereinafter, “the SIT”). It is not in
dispute that the said report formed part of the writ
petition/ public interest litigation which has now been
dismissed in default, resulting in the vacation of all
interim orders passed therein. During the pendency of the
said  writ  petition,  further  show  case  notices  and
consequential orders of termination were issued. These
actions were challenged by the appellants before the High
Court in one or more rounds of litigation.
20

--- Page 25 ---
3) Since the date of appointment, the appellants are
continuing till now under the orders of the Court.  It is
not out of place to observe that all these appellants
have served between five to fifteen years approximately,
and during such period, they have been confirmed and some
of them were promoted as well. However, the recourse of
termination, inter alia observing that the documents were
not  proper,  be  taken  at  least  after  ensuring  the
procedure prescribed duly followed.  
4) It has been brought to our notice that Section 67 of
the  Uttar  Pradesh  State  Universities  Act,  1973
(hereinafter “1973 Act”) contemplates compliance to the
principles of natural justice before any adverse action
has  been  taken  against  a  confirmed  employee.  The
respondents, however, contended that the provisions of
the 1973 Act would not apply since the issue concerning
the validity and cancellation of the degrees on the basis
of  which  the  appellants  were  appointed  is  under
consideration. In our view, the question whether the
provisions of the 1973 Act are attracted to the present
case can appropriately be determined by the competent
authority  while  examining  the  allegations  levelled
against the appellants and also the validity of the
21

--- Page 26 ---
action  proposed  to  be  taken  against  them.  What  is,
however, beyond dispute is that the orders of termination
were passed without the appellants being afforded an
adequate opportunity of hearing and in observance of the
principles of natural justice. Having regard to the fact
that the termination orders were passed long ago yet have
remained unimplemented due to the interim orders of this
Court; and considering that the controversy persisted
largely on account of non-observance of the procedure
prescribed by the respondent. 
5) In the facts, we are of the opinion that it would be
appropriate to continue the interim protection as granted
by this Court giving liberty to the State Government to
take recourse under the provisions of the 1973 Act after
affording an opportunity to the appellants, indicating
the  allegations  and  asking  their  reply,  whereafter,
appropriate orders ought be passed in conformity to the
observance of principles of natural justice.  
6) In  view  of  the  foregoing,  at  present,  without
commenting on the findings as recorded in the order
impugned, for all practical purposes, maintaining the
stay order on termination for the teachers who have
served for a considerable time period and some of them
22

--- Page 27 ---
have been granted promotion, it is tough to confirm the
impugned order at this stage. Since the fact-finding
inquiry with participation of the affected teachers has
not come on record with respect to the individual cases
and the action is being taken merely in terms of the
orders passed by the High Court and the interim report of
the SIT, therefore, it would be in the fitness of things
that all the parties be given adequate opportunity of
hearing  by  following  the  procedure,  leaving  all  the
questions open to be raised by either side.  
7) In view of the foregoing, we dispose of these appeals
with the following directions: 
(i) In  the  facts  and  circumstances  of  this
case, the impugned order passed by the High
Court stands set aside. The consequential
action of termination also stands set aside
at this stage. 
(ii) The State Government is at liberty to take
recourse as permissible. We make it clear
that  while  taking  such  recourse,  the
allegations as levelled against individual
employees shall be enquired into in the
manner  as  prescribed,  and  observing  the
23

--- Page 28 ---
principles  of  natural  justice  prior  to
passing the final order. The intent of this
Court is that the appellants/petitioners’
civil  right  is  going  to  be  affected
therefore,  they  should  not  be  condemned
unheard.  In  case  it  is  found  that  the
procedure prescribed in the 1973 Act does
not apply, due opportunity of hearing ought
to be given. The interim protection granted
by this Court shall remain in operation
subject to the outcome of the orders of the
competent authority. Parties are at liberty
to raise all the points as available to
them. 
8) In view of the above, the civil appeals stand disposed
of.  Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.
CRIMINAL APPEAL NOS. 4217/2024 AND 4218/2024
(1) These criminal appeals assail the respective orders
of the High Court whereby the petitions filed by the
appellants  seeking  quashing  of  the  respective  FIRs
registered  against  them,  alleging  use  of  forged  or
tampered degrees, came to be dismissed. 
24

--- Page 29 ---
(2) Criminal Appeal No. 4217 of 2024 pertains to Case
Crime No. 178 of 2020 dated 14.07.2020 registered at
Police Station Arwakatra, District Auraiya under Sections
409, 420, 467, 468, 471, 204, 201 and 120-B of IPC and
Sections 13(1)(d)(ii) and 13(1)(d)(iii) of the Prevention
of Corruption Act, 1988 against the appellant Umesh Kumar
Sharma. 
(3) Criminal Appeal No. 4218 of 2024 pertains to FIR No.
526 of 2022 dated 06.07.2022 registered at Police Station
Kotwali City, District Hardoi under Sections 419, 420,
467, 468 and 471 of IPC against the appellant Brijendra
Pal.
(4) The allegations forming the basis of the FIRs are
intrinsically connected with the controversy which formed
the  subject  matter  of  the  connected  civil  appeals
disposed  of  by  us  today.  By  the  decision  rendered
therein, this Court has directed the competent authority
to examine the allegations against the appellants afresh,
after affording them due opportunity of hearing and in
compliance with the principles of natural justice. 
(5) Since  the  foundational  issue  regarding  the
authenticity  and  validity  of  the  educational
qualifications relied upon by the appellants is yet to
25

--- Page 30 ---
attain finality and is required to be determined pursuant
to the directions issued in the connected matters, we are
of the view that it would not be appropriate for the
criminal proceedings to proceed further at this stage.
(6) Accordingly, without expressing any opinion on the
merits of the allegations contained in the FIRs, we
direct that all further proceedings arising out of the
respective  FIRs,  as  mentioned  above,  including  any
consequential proceedings, shall remain in abeyance till
the  competent  authority  passes  appropriate  orders
pursuant to the directions issued by this Court in the
connected civil appeals. Thereafter, it shall be open to
the investigating agency and all concerned parties to
take such steps as may be permissible in law, depending
upon the outcome of the proceedings before the competent
authority.
(7) These criminal appeals are disposed of in the above
terms.

26

petitioners  on  allegations  pertaining  to  the  civil

(2) In view of the directions of this Court in the civil

REPORTABLE
IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO.            OF 2026
(Arising out of Special Leave Petition (Crl.) No.4727 of 2026)
JITTU YADAV                                               …APPELLANT
VERSUS
STATE OF CHHATTISGARH & OTHERS    …RESPONDENTS
OPERATIVE PORTION OF THE JUDGMENT 
NAGARATHNA, J.
Leave granted.
It is noted that challenge to the order of externment
dated 18.06.2025 passed by the District Magistrate, District
Balodabazar-Bhatapara which was appealed against before the
State Government was dismissed on the ground of delay vide
order dated 03.10.2025. The same was challenged before the
High Court of Chhattisgarh at Bilaspur in WPCR No.548 of
2025  and  also  came  to  be  dismissed  vide  judgment  dated
3

--- Page 54 ---
16.10.2025. We have considered the correctness of the said
order in light of the provisions of the Limitation Act, 1963 (for
short,  “Limitation  Act”),  particularly,  Sections  29(2)  and  5
thereof. We propose to allow the appeal and restore the appeal
filed  by  the  appellant  herein  before  the  State  Government
under  Section  9  of  the  Chhattisgarh  Rajya  Suraksha
Adhiniyam, 1990 (for short, “Adhiniyam”), so as to be disposed
of in accordance with law. 
In view of the ensuing summer vacation/partial Court
working days of this Court commencing from 01.06.2026 and
the  last  working  day  prior  thereto  being  29.05.2026,  on
allowing this appeal, we propose to indicate only the operative
portion of our judgment and release the detailed judgment
later, so that the appeal filed by the appellant herein before
the State Government is restored and is heard on merits as
the period of externment is ending on 18.06.2026. We hence
indicate the operative portion of our judgment as under:
“In our view, both from the text of Section 9 and from
the overall statutory scheme of the Adhiniyam, there
4

--- Page 55 ---
is  no  indication  that  the  legislature  intended  to
exclude the operation of Section 5 of the Limitation
Act. There is no contra provision in the Adhiniyam
expressly  for  not  condoning  the  delay  if  an
application  is filed  beyond  thirty  days under  sub-
section  (1)  of  Section  9  of  the  Adhiniyam.  In  the
absence  of  such  exclusion,  Section  5  of  the
Limitation Act operates, and delay in filing the appeal
can be condoned upon sufficient cause being shown
in accordance with Section 5 of the Limitation Act.
In the result, we conclude as follows:
a. Section  9  of  the  Adhiniyam  does  not  bar  the
application of Section 5 of the Limitation Act.
b. No application under Section 5 of the Limitation
Act seeking condonation of delay being before the
State Government, the application for directions
filed by the appellant being Crl. M.P. No. 150947
of 2026 before this Court is taken on record and
5

--- Page 56 ---
is  allowed.  The  delay  in  filing  the  appeal  is
condoned.
c. Accordingly,  the  appeal  before  the  State
Government under Section 9 of the Adhiniyam
stands restored and shall be decided on its own
merits  and  in  accordance  with  law  as
expeditiously as possible and at any rate on or
before  15.06.2026.  The  appellant  shall  appear
before the State Government on 01.06.2026.
d. Resultantly,  the  Impugned  Judgment  dated
16.10.2025  passed  by  the  High  Court  of
Chhattisgarh at Bilaspur  in  WPCR No. 548 of
2025 is set aside.
The appeal stands disposed of in the aforesaid terms.
Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand disposed
of.”
…………………………………..J.
   (B.V. NAGARATHNA)
6

--- Page 57 ---
…………………………………..J.
   (UJJAL BHUYAN)
NEW DELHI;
MAY 27, 2026.

ITEM NO.20               COURT NO.4               SECTION II-B
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CRIMINAL) Diary No(s). 33772/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 30-03-2022
in JCRLA No. 74/2011 passed by the High Court of Orissa at Cuttack]
KULAMANI BEHERA                                    Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF ODISHA                                    Respondent(s)
(IA No. 176255/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN FILING)
 
Date : 23-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE UJJAL BHUYAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ARUN PALLI
[Partial Court Working Days Bench]
For Petitioner(s): Ms. Rukhsana Choudhury, AOR                   
                   
For Respondent(s): 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for the petitioner.
2. Petitioner has been convicted under Section 302 of
the Indian Penal Code, 1860 (IPC) and sentenced to
undergo life imprisonment. His appeal was rejected by
the High Court.
3. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that
petitioner  has  already  undergone  17  years  of
imprisonment.
4. Considering the period of custody undergone by the
petitioner, we are of the view that present is a fit
case where petitioner’s case for remission may be
1

--- Page 65 ---
considered by the State. In this regard we may refer to
the decision of this Court in In Re: Policy Strategy
for Grant of Bail1, the relevant portion of which reads
thus:
“21. We,  therefore,  record  the  following
conclusions:
a) Where there is a policy of the appropriate
Government  laying  down  guidelines  for
consideration of the grant of premature release
under Section 432 of the CrPC or Section 473 of
the  BNSS,  it  is  the  obligation  of  the
appropriate Government to consider cases of all
convicts for grant of premature release as and
when they become eligible for consideration in
terms of the policy. In such a case, it is not
necessary for the convict or his relatives to
make  a  specific  application  for  grant  of
permanent remission. When the jail manual or
any other departmental instruction issued by
the appropriate Government contains such policy
guidelines, the aforesaid direction will apply;
b) We direct those States and Union Territories
that do not have a policy dealing with the
grant of remission in terms of Section  432 of
the CrPC or  Section  473  of  the  BNSS  to
formulate  a  policy  within  two  months  from
today;
c) Appropriate Government has the power to
incorporate suitable conditions in an order
granting permanent remission. Consideration of
various factors, which are mentioned in the
paragraph 13 above by way of illustration, is
necessary before finalizing the conditions. The
conditions  must  aim  at  ensuring  that  the
1  2025 SCC OnLine SC 349
2

--- Page 66 ---
criminal tendencies, if any, of the convict
remain  in  check  and  that  the  convict
rehabilitates  himself  in  the  society.  The
conditions  should  not  be  so  oppressive  or
stringent that the convict is not able to take
advantage  of  the  order  granting  permanent
remission. The conditions cannot be vague and
should be capable of being performed;
d) Order granting or refusing the relief of
permanent remission must contain brief reasons.
The  order  containing  reasons  should  be
immediately communicated to the convict through
the office of the concerned prison. The copies
thereof should be forwarded to the Secretaries
of  the  concerned  District  Legal  Services
Authorities. It is the duty of the prison
authorities to inform the convict that he has
the right to challenge the order of rejection
of the prayer for the grant of remission.
e) As held in the case of  Mafabhai Motibhai
Sagar4, an order granting permanent remission
cannot be withdrawn or cancelled without giving
an opportunity of being heard to the convict.
An order of cancellation of permanent remission
must contain brief reasons;
f)  The  District  Legal  Services  Authorities
shall endeavour to implement NALSA SOP in its
true letter and spirit.
g)  Further,  the  District  Legal  Services
Authorities shall also monitor implementation
of conclusion (a) as recorded above. For this
purpose,  the  District  Legal  Services
Authorities shall maintain the relevant date of
the  convicts  and  as  and  when  they  become
eligible  to  a  consideration  for  grant  of
3

--- Page 67 ---
premature release, they shall do the needful in
terms  of  conclusion  (a).  The  State  Legal
Services Authorities shall endeavour to create
a portal on which the data as aforesaid can be
uploaded on real time basis.”
5. In terms of the aforesaid judgment, we direct the
State of Odisha to consider the case of the petitioner
expeditiously for permanent remission in terms of the
applicable policy.
6. The Odisha State Legal Services Authority shall do
the  needful  in  this  regard  through  the  concerned
District Legal Services Authority.
7. We also take note of the fact that there is a huge
delay of 1489 days in filing the present Special Leave
Petition. Notwithstanding the same, we have considered
the present Special Leave Petition and have passed the
aforesaid order.
8. With this observation, the Special Leave Petition
is disposed of.
9. Pending application(s) including the application
for condonation of delay, if any, shall stand disposed
of.
(ABHINAV KUMAR)                                 (SAPNA BANSAL)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

--- Page 68 ---

Date : 23-06-2026 This petition was called on for hearing today.

For Petitioner(s) : Mr. M.P. Parthiban, AOR                   
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel, the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
The  petitioner-Registrar,  Madurai  Kamaraj  University
(hereinafter  being  referred  to  as  the  “University”)  has
approached this Court by way of the instant special leave
petition seeking to assail the order dated 23 rd March, 2026
passed by the Division Bench of the Madras High Court,
Madurai Bench in C.M.P.(MD) No. 3795 of 2026 in W.A.(MD)
1

--- Page 69 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21980/2026
SR. No. 22727 of 2026.
The petitioner had preferred the aforesaid writ appeal
challenging the order dated 19 th April, 2022 passed by the
learned  Single  Judge  in  W.P.  (MD)  No.  2096  of  2020
whereby the learned Single Judge accepted the writ petition
preferred by respondent No. 1-B. Shivakumar and directed
the University to count the services of respondent No. 1 for
the entire period of his engagement including the services
rendered from February 1990 to 2005 in the post of Senior
Technical Assistant, with the petitioner-University. The writ
appeal was filed with a delay of 1368 days.  
An application under Section 5 of the Limitation Act,
1963 was moved with the writ appeal.  The learned Division
Bench,  perused  the  grounds  set  out  in  the  application
seeking  condonation  of delay  and  found  the same to  be
absolutely unacceptable.
We  have  also  perused  the  grounds  raised  in  the
application  seeking  condonation  of  delay  filed  before  the
Division Bench and found the same to be perfunctory, to
say the least.  The petitioner-University has dragged the
2

--- Page 70 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21980/2026
pensioner  employee  (respondent  No.  1)  to  the  Division
Bench and thereafter to this Court for an issue which ought
not  to  have  been  dragged  to  litigation.  Indisputably,
respondent No. 1 had worked with the petitioner-University
between February 1990 and 2005.  He sought permission to
serve in another institution which was denied to him and
thereafter,  respondent  No.  1  was  granted  a  fresh
appointment  letter  from  2007  onwards.   Apparently,  the
said  break  in  service  was  artificial  and  caused  grave
prejudice to the employee who had put in almost 15 years’
service. The petitioner-University could not have denied the
benefit  of  the  said  period  as  qualifying  service  for  the
purpose of calculating terminal and pensionary benefits.
We, therefore, find no  cause to entertain the special
leave petition which is dismissed with costs quantified at
Rs.50,000/-.
The petitioner-University shall pay the said cost to the
respondent  No.  1-B.  Shivakumar  within  a  period  of  six
weeks from today and present a receipt of payment in the
Registry  of  the  High  Court.   In  case  the  receipt  is  not
3

--- Page 71 ---
SLP (C)  NO. 21980/2026
presented  within  6  weeks,  the  High  Court  shall  take
necessary steps for the recovery of the said amount from the
petitioner-University  and  ensure  payment  thereof  to
respondent No. 1-B. Shivakumar.
A  copy  of  the  order  be  transmitted  to  the  Registrar
General of the Madras High Court, Madurai Bench.
Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.
(POOJA SHARMA)                                  (NIDHI WASON)

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO.        OF 2026
(Arising out of SLP (Criminal) No. 8611 of 2026)
WASIM RAHMAN   APPELLANT(S)
VERSUS
STATE OF UTTAR PRADESH  RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. The appellant is aggrieved by the impugned order
passed by the High Court, refusing to suspend the sentence
imposed upon him by the Trial Court for committing offence
punishable under Sections 323 and 304 (Part-II) read with
Section 34 of Indian Penal Code, 1860 and has been awarded
maximum sentence of rigorous imprisonment for three years
and fine of Rs. 25,000/- for the offence punishable under
Section 304 (Part-II) of IPC.
3. The appeal preferred by the appellant pending before
the Allahabad High Court is of the year 2026 and the
maximum sentence awarded is rigorous imprisonment for three
years, out of which the appellant has already undergone
rigorous imprisonment for six months.
4. Having considered all the relevant aspects of the
1

--- Page 77 ---
matter, particularly considering the fact that the disposal
of the appeal may take some time in the High Court and by
the  time  appeal  is  heard,  the  appellant  would  have
undergone the entire sentence, we think it is a fit case
for interference.
5. In the above view of the matter, we allow the
appeal, set aside the impugned order dated 16.04.2026, and
direct the suspension of the sentence imposed upon the
appellant by the Trial Court, and direct him to be released
on bail in connection with FIR No. 02 of 2020, registered
at Police Station-Rampur, District-Jaunpur (Uttar Pradesh),
for the offence punishable under Sections 323 and 304
(Part-II) read with Section 34 of IPC, subject to such
terms and conditions as may be imposed by the Trial Court.
6. The appeal is allowed in the above terms.
7. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO. 114 OF 2018
 STATE OF UTTAR PRADESH                    APPELLANT(S)
                                VERSUS
 JAI PRAKASH DUBEY                   RESPONDENT(S)
  
     O R D E R  
1. The  appellant  challenges  the  judgment  and  order  dated
31.03.2017 passed in Criminal Appeal No.4603 of 2013 titled “ Jai
Prakash Dubey vs. State of U.P .” passed by the High Court of
Judicature at Allahabad.
2. By the impugned judgment, the High Court reversed the findings
of fact returned by the Trial Court (Additional Sessions Judge,
Court No. 3, Mau) vide judgment dated 04.10.2013. The Trial Court,
while convicting and sentencing the respondent, Jai Prakash Dubey,
for having committed offences under Sections 304-B and 498-A of
the Indian Penal Code (IPC), acquitted the co-accused, namely
Hansnath Dubey, Smt. Parwati, Smt. Manju, Smt. Reena, and Smt.
Bandana, by granting them the benefit of doubt on all counts.
3. The High Court, in terms of the impugned judgment, set aside
the conviction and sentence of the respondent.
4. Having heard learned counsel for the parties and perused the
records made available, we are of the considered view that no
ground for interference is made out in the present appeal.
5. In our view, the High Court, after fully appreciating the
1

--- Page 81 ---
evidence led by the parties, correctly reversed the findings of
fact returned by the Trial Court. The High Court, being first
Court  of  Appeal,  fully  appreciated  the  testimonies  of  the
prosecution witnesses, specifically, PW-1, brother of the deceased
and PW-2, mother of the deceased.
6. Undoubtedly,  there  exists  a  statutory  presumption  under
Section 113-B of the Evidence Act. Nonetheless, in our considered
view, the same stood rebutted by the accused, as the offence
cannot be said to have taken place “soon before” or “immediately
before” the occurrence of the incident.
7. The findings of fact that the death of the deceased was
suicidal and not homicidal cannot be said to be perverse.  As per
the medical evidence, the deceased died from consuming Aluminium
Phosphide (sulphas), and the post-mortem report noted no external
or internal injury marks on the dead body. The testimony of doctor
(PW-3) is evidentiary clear on this count. While the prosecution
led evidence through PW-1 and PW-2 i.e. brother and mother of the
deceased respectively, to establish dowry demands, the High Court
correctly found lack of supportive evidence.
8. In our considered view, the High Court correctly concluded
that the respondent’s conviction by the Trial Court was based on
the same set of evidence that was found insufficient to convict
the other co-accused. The conviction was set aside due to a lack
of supportive evidence for the alleged acts.
9. The appeal stands dismissed.
2

--- Page 82 ---
10. Pending applications, if any, shall stand disposed of.
.......................J.  
                                      (SANJAY KAROL)              
  .......................J.
               (AUGUSTINE GEORGE MASIH)    
  NEW DELHI;
  JUNE 03, 2026
3

--- Page 83 ---

ITEM NO.27               COURT NO.6               SECTION II-B
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CRIMINAL) Diary No(s). 31129/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 30-01-2026
in CRMM No. 27538/2025 passed by the High Court of Punjab & Haryana
at Chandigarh]
ABC & ANR.                                         Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF PUNJAB & ORS.                             Respondent(s)
(IA No. 179950/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN FILING
IA No. 179949/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
IA No. 179948/2026 - PERMISSION TO FILE ADDITIONAL 
DOCUMENTS/FACTS/ANNEXURES)
 
Date : 24-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE SANDEEP MEHTA
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE N.V. ANJARIA
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) : 
                   Mr. Vikas Verma, AOR
                   Ms. Sapna Verma, Adv.
                   Mr. Shafik Ahmed, Adv.
                   Ms. Kavita Verma, Adv.
                   Ms. Priya Verma, Adv.
                   Ms. Anju, Adv.
                   Mr. Rishab Sardana, Adv.
                   Dr. Vinod Kumar Goyal, Adv.                   
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Delay condoned.
2. Heard  learned  counsel  for  the  petitioners  and
perused the material available on record.
1

--- Page 92 ---
3. The petitioners seek transfer of proceedings of
Criminal case bearing Sessions Case No.255 of 2024 titled
“State of Punjab v. Rajat Kumar” arising out of FIR No.35
of 2024 dated 12th June, 2024 registered at Police Station
Sadar Abohar, District Fazilka, Punjab pending in the
Court of the Additional Sessions Judge, Fazilka, Punjab
to a Court of competent jurisdiction at Chandigarh.
4. We are of the view that the petitioners being
complainant and the victim of the case, cannot dictate
terms as to where the trial should be held.  Initially,
Zero FIR was registered at Chandigarh and then the same
was transferred to Fazilka because the alleged offence
took place at Fazilka.  Most of the witnesses cited in
the criminal case would be from Fazilka.  The High Court
has observed that the allegations of threat perception
raised by the petitioners in support of the prayer for
transfer were not substantiated.  In any event, the so
called threat perception expressed by the petitioners can
be taken care of by directing the Trial Court to provide
security to the petitioners when they are summoned to
give evidence.  The High Court has assigned valid reasons
for  refusing  the  prayer  for  transfer  made  by  the
petitioners.  The impugned order does not suffer from any
infirmity warranting interference by this Court.
2

--- Page 93 ---
5. With these observations, the Special Leave Petition
fails and is dismissed as being devoid of merit.
6. A copy of this order shall be transmitted to the
Trial Court so that, appropriate security measures can be
provided to the witnesses i.e. the petitioners herein
when they are summoned to depose before the Trial Court.
7. Pending applications shall also stand disposed of.
(ANITA MALHOTRA)                          (NIDHI WASON)
     DEPUTY REGISTRAR                       ASSISTANT REGISTRAR
3

--- Page 94 ---
ITEM NO.10               COURT NO.6               SECTION XIV

Date : 24-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :

         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE N.V. ANJARIA
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) : 
                   Mr. Rakesh Dahiya, AOR
                   Mr. Aakash Dahiya, Adv.
                   Mr. Aditya Dahiya, Adv.                   
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
                   Mr. Amit Bajaj,Adv.
                   Ms. Vagisha Kochar, AOR                   
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Mr. Amit Bajaj, learned counsel puts in appearance
on behalf of the respondent, on caveat.  Thus, notice
need not be issued.
2. With the consent of the parties, the matter has
been heard finally.
1

--- Page 95 ---
3.  The petitioner-husband is before us by way of the
instant petition for assailing the judgment and order
dated 11th May, 2026 passed by the High Court of Delhi in
C.M.(M) No.324 of 2026.
4. The respondent-wife filed a petition under Sections
13(1)(ia) and 13(1)(ib) of the Hindu Marriage Act, 1955
seeking a decree of divorce on the grounds of cruelty and
desertion before the Family Court, Tis Hazari Courts,
Delhi.   The  petitioner  failed  to  cross-examine  the
respondent on which, the right to cross-examination was
closed by the Family Court in May, 2024.  The said order
was  subsequently recalled  on payment  of cost.   The
petitioner thereafter, filed his affidavit of evidence,
but  failed  to  remain  present  for  cross-examination,
despite multiple opportunities on which, the evidence of
the petitioner was closed by the Family Court vide order
dated 15th December, 2025.  The said order was assailed by
the  petitioner  by  filing  the  subject  Miscellaneous
Application before the High Court which stands rejected
by order dated 11 th May, 2026 under challenge in the
present petition.
5. Having heard the learned counsel for the parties
and considered the submissions advanced and after going
through the material on record, we feel that one further
opportunity with a window of 30 days deserves to be
2

--- Page 96 ---
extended to the petitioner to lead his evidence in the
divorce proceedings.
6. This indulgence would, however, be subject to the
petitioner’s depositing a sum of Rs.50,000/- (Rupees
fifty thousand) by way of cost with the Family Court and
also  clearing  the  complete  arrears  of  maintenance
awarded to the minor child of the parties.  The aforesaid
amounts shall be deposited by the petitioner with the
Family Court within a period of two months from today and
shall be disbursed to the respondent-wife.  Thereafter,
the Family Court shall fix one date for recording of the
evidence  of  the  petitioner  and  his  witnesses  which
process shall be completed within a period of 30 days
thereafter.
7. The Special Leave Petition is disposed of in these
terms.
8. Pending applications shall also stand disposed of.
(ANITA MALHOTRA)                          (NIDHI WASON)
     DEPUTY REGISTRAR                       ASSISTANT REGISTRAR

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Since the petitioner’s Writ Petition(s) and his
prayer for interim relief is pending consideration before
the High Court, we do not want to enter into the merits
of the matter, as the same would affect the contentions
of either of the parties before the High Court.
2. At the same time, we are of the view that the High
Court should have passed orders on petitioner’s prayer
for interim relief, otherwise on or after 30.06.2026, the
Writ Petition(s) shall be rendered infructuous.
2

--- Page 99 ---
3. In the above view of the matter, we dispose of the
Special Leave Petition(s), directing the petitioner to
move an application for preponement of hearing, for
deciding his prayer for interim relief on merits.
4. In the meanwhile, till the petitioner’s prayer for
interim relief is considered and decided by the High
Court, the parties shall maintain status quo in respect
of the subject matter of the Writ Petition(s).
5. We request the High Court to decide the matter(s)
expeditiously.
6. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.

that she is his sister. M.Sandeep Bothra-contemnor no.2 is
not present, it is informed that he is recently been
married.

2
we request to Ms.Haripriya Padmanabhan, learned Senior

curiae along with AOR Ms.Pooja Dhar on behalf of the
